Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia (Redirected from NBA regular season records ) "NBA records" and "List of NBA records" redirect here. For NBA playoff and Finals records, see List of NBA postseason records . For All-Star records, see List of NBA All-Star Game records .

This article lists all-time records achieved in the NBA regular season in major statistical categories recognized by the league, including those set by teams and individuals in a game, season, and career. The NBA also recognizes records from its original incarnation, the Basketball Association of America (BAA).

Awards Most Total selections to the All-NBA Team LeBron James with 21 selections [ 1 ] Most First-team selections to the All-NBA Team LeBron James with 13 selections [ 2 ] Most MVPs Kareem Abdul-Jabbar with 6 selections [ 3 ] Most Total selections to the All-Defensive Team Tim Duncan with 15 selections [ 4 ] Most First-team selections to the All-Defensive Team Michael Jordan , Gary Payton , Kevin Garnett and Kobe Bryant with 9 selections [ 5 ] Most Defensive Player of the Year Awards Dikembe Mutombo , Ben Wallace , and Rudy Gobert , tied with 4 selections [ 6 ] Most Sixth Man of the Year Awards Jamal Crawford and Lou Williams , tied with 3 selections [ 7 ] Most Hustle Awards Marcus Smart with 3 selections [ 8 ] Most Teammate of the Year Awards Jrue Holiday with 3 selections [ 9 ] Most Sportsmanship Awards Mike Conley Jr.

with 4 selections [ 10 ] Most Coach of the Year Awards Don Nelson , Pat Riley , and Gregg Popovich , tied with 3 selections [ 11 ] Most Executive of the Year Awards Jerry Colangelo , with 4 selections Year , Defensive Player of the Year, and MVP awards Michael Jordan and David Robinson [ 15 ] [ 16 ] Only players to win Rookie of the Year and MVP in the same season Wes Unseld ( 1968–69 ) and Wilt Chamberlain ( 1959–60 ) [ 17 ] [ 18 ] Only player to win the Scoring Title and Defensive Player of the Year in the same season Michael Jordan , 1987–88 [ 19 ] Only players to win Rookie of the Year and Sixth Man of the Year Awards Mike Miller and Malcolm Brogdon [ 20 ] Only rookie to make the All-Defensive First Team Victor Wembanyama , 2023–24 [ 21 ] Shortest player to make the All-NBA team Blake Griffin , Damian Lillard , Karl-Anthony Towns with 6 selections Individual career records LeBron James is the all-time leader in a number of categories, including most seasons played , most career points , and nearly every individual playoff statistic.

Dirk Nowitzki played all 21 of his NBA seasons with the Dallas Mavericks , the most seasons played with a single franchise.

Green [ 38 ] Most games played on one team, career 1,522 by Dirk Nowitzki [ 39 ] Most minutes played, career 57,447 by LeBron James (active) Most minutes per game averaged, career 45.8 by Wilt Chamberlain [ 40 ] Most triple-doubles, career 203 by Russell Westbrook (active) [ 41 ] Most 50–40–90 seasons, career 4 by Steve Nash between 2005 and 2010 [ 42 ] [ 43 ] Points Statistics accurate as of the 2024–25 NBA season .

1996–97) -58 by Scoot Henderson on March 29, 2024 [ 738 ] Rookie and age-related records In 2006, the NBA introduced age requirement restrictions. Prospective high school players must wait a year before entering the NBA, making age-related records harder to break.

Youngest player debut Andrew Bynum (18 years, 6 days) with the Los Angeles Lakers against the Denver Nuggets on November 2, 2005 .

[ 739 ] Oldest player debut Nat Hickey (45 years, 362 days) with the Providence Steamrollers against the St. Louis Bombers on January 27, 1949 . He was the team's coach and activated himself as a player. He only played 2 games.

Largest comeback 36 points (:20 left in 2nd) – The Utah Jazz overcame a 36-point deficit [ 888 ] to defeat the Denver Nuggets at home on November 27, 1996 .

[ 889 ] Utah trailed 70–34 with 20 seconds left in the 1st half, but outscored Denver 73–33 during the rest of the game to win 107–103. This is the largest overall deficit overcome in NBA history.
